    john hanna reposted this
    Paul Nicolaou • 3rd+ Executive Director at Business Sydney 1d •
    Sydney continues to strengthen its position as a global centre for innovation, talent and technology. Last week, more than 100 business leaders, academics and industry representatives joined Business Sydney and UNSW Sydney for an exclusive luncheon exploring the transformative potential of artificial intelligence for business, society and the future of work.

    At a time when digital literacy and AI capability are becoming essential drivers of competitiveness, workforce development and economic resilience, the discussion highlighted the importance of strong collaboration between industry and academia. We were honoured to hear from Professor Attila Brungs, Vice-Chancellor and President of UNSW Sydney, who delivered a thought-provoking keynote on the critical role universities play in advancing AI research, innovation and talent development, and how partnerships between universities and business will help shape Australia’s future prosperity.

    A special thank you to Tarushi Nandwani, UNSW Data Science and Decisions student and former President of the UNSW AI Society, for sharing an inspiring next-generation perspective on the opportunities AI presents for students and future workforces.

    A highlight of the event was the engaging panel discussion facilitated by Professor Paul Andon, Dean of UNSW Business School, featuring:

    ⭐️ Professor Fahim Khondaker, Partner, Data and AI, BDO Australia

    ⭐️ Renay Ringma, Head of AI, AMP

    ⭐️ Minnie Singh-Murphy, Executive Manager, AI Education, Partnerships and Adoption, Westpac

    The panel explored the practical application of AI across industries, emerging opportunities for business growth, workforce readiness, responsible adoption, governance considerations and the evolving skills required to succeed in an AI-enabled economy.

    We also extend our sincere thanks to
    Christina Larkin, Digital Assurance Leader at EY, for delivering the vote of thanks and helping conclude a highly insightful discussion.

    Business Sydney is proud to partner with UNSW Sydney to foster meaningful conversations that connect business, education and innovation. Together, we can help build an AI-capable workforce, support lifelong learning and ensure Sydney remains at the forefront of the opportunities presented by the digital economy.

  • Feed post number 2

    john hanna • 3rd+ Executive Leadership ♦ Chief Information Officer ♦ Co-Founder Non-Executive Director ♦ Passion for Transforming Complex Ecosystems ♦ Purpose and People ♦ Aficionado of Horological Artistry and Alfa Romeos
    View my blog
    1d •
    A strong and timely perspective. Agentic AI will not be won through experimentation alone, it will be won through architecture, discipline and operational maturity. The real shift is not simply moving from chatbots to agents, but designing workflows that can reason, act, validate, recover and improve within trusted enterprise boundaries. That means clear agent roles, well-defined tools, memory, orchestration, observability, governance and human accountability from day one.
    For leaders, the opportunity is significant — but so is the responsibility. Agentic AI should not become another layer of technical theatre. It must solve real business problems, integrate with real systems, operate with real controls, and earn trust through measurable outcomes. The organisations that succeed will be those that combine imagination with engineering rigour — turning AI from a clever interface into a genuine operating capability.
    hashtag#AgenticAI hashtag#AIArchitecture hashtag#DigitalTransformation hashtag#EnterpriseAI hashtag#Automation hashtag#Leadership hashtag#Innovation hashtag#ResponsibleAI
    Agentic AI Leadership
    A Simple Guide on Architecting End-to-End Agentic AI Workflows
    Sanjoy Kumar Malik

    Henrique Braun • 3rd+ Chief Executive Officer of The Coca-Cola Company 3d •
    This week, I spent time with a group of global leaders from across The Coca-Cola Company, focused on one question: how we build what comes next.

    Inflection moments take shape in companies with long histories when people choose to see around corners and move with clarity and conviction.

    I see us at that kind of moment now. How we shape the future comes from three connected ideas.

    1. Get closer to the consumer. Using sharper insights, stronger innovation and tighter integration to serve people better.

    2. Place digital at the core of how we work. Every connection, every decision and every interaction becomes an opportunity to move faster and operate with greater precision.

    3. Stay constructively discontent. Keep raising the bar a little more, a little better, every day, everywhere.

    I am energized by the momentum in our business, the strength of our system and the power of our brands. Most of all, I am inspired by our people and the way they come together to shape the next chapter of growth for our company.
